Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Introduction to al-Ghazali and Mahakk al-Nazar
Title page introducing the book and its author, Imam al-Ghazali.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author and the title of the foundational text of Islamic logic, Mahakk al-Nazar.

Core Idea
Al-Ghazali, the Proof of Islam, authored Mahakk al-Nazar to establish the criteria for sound argumentation.

This title page introduces the book you are about to study and its illustrious author, Imam al-Ghazali. As a towering figure in Islamic theology, jurisprudence, and philosophy, al-Ghazali's works on logic are essential for anyone seeking to distinguish truth from falsehood in Islamic sciences. Understanding the source and its background will help you contextualize the logical tools you will learn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's full name and titles
Locate the name 'Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Ghazali' and the honorifics 'Hujjat al-Islam' (Proof of Islam) and 'Zayn al-Din' (Ornament of the Religion). These titles indicate his high scholarly status.
The name includes lineage back to his grandfather Ahmad, confirming his identity.
2
Identify the book title
The title is given as 'ف الف النظرة', which is an OCR corruption of 'محاك النظارة' or 'Mahakk al-Nazar' (The Touchstone of Argument). This work is a concise introduction to logic.
The correct title is confirmed by scholarly tradition.
3
Note his school, birthplace, and lifespan
The text mentions his Shafi'i school affiliation, birthplace (Tusi/Tabarani), and lifespan (450-505 AH / 1058-1111 CE). These details help place him in Islamic intellectual history.
Al-Ghazali lived during the Seljuk era and was a key figure in the Ash'ari theological school.
4
Recognize the significance
Al-Ghazali was instrumental in integrating Aristotelian logic into Islamic theology, using it to defend orthodox beliefs against philosophical objections. Mahakk al-Nazar is one of his introductory logical works.
His works on logic paved the way for later scholars like Fakhr al-Din al-Razi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ف الف النظرة تأليف الإمام المجدد حجة الإسلام والمسلمين زين الدين أبي حامد محمد بن محمد بن محمد بن أحمد الغزالي الطوسي الطابراني الشافعي رضي الله عنه (٤٥٠-٥٠٥ هـ) دار المنه
In the Look/Consideration. Authored by the renewing Imam, the proof of Islam and Muslims, Zayn al-Din, Abu Hamid Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Ghazali al-Tusi al-Tabarani al-Shafi'i, may Allah be pleased with him (450-505 AH). Dar al-Manha.
Source pages p. 1

Commentary
This passage is the title page of al-Ghazali's logical treatise 'Mahakk al-Nazar' (The Touchstone of Argument). It identifies the author as the renowned scholar Abu Hamid al-Ghazali (1058-1111 CE), a towering figure in Islamic theology, jurisprudence, and philosophy. The text gives his full name, lineage, and honorific titles, including 'the Proof of Islam' and 'the Renewer of the Religion.' It also notes his school (Shafi'i) and birthplace (Tusi/Tabarani). The date range (450-505 AH) confirms his lifespan. The publisher's name is partially illegible but likely refers to a modern printing house.

A) Ibn Sina

Key Takeaway
Al-Ghazali's Mahakk al-Nazar is his introductory treatise on logic, serving as a touchstone for valid reasoning in Islamic sciences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify the author and title of this work. Then, in one sentence, explain why al-Ghazali is called 'Hujjat al-Islam' (the Proof of Islam).

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Parsing a Classical Title Page: Mahakk al-Nazar
Title page with author's full name, honorifics, and publication info.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and interpret the key components of a classical Islamic title page, including the author's full name, honorifics, and subject matter.

Core Idea
A title page is a gateway to a book's authority and purpose.

When you open a classical Islamic work, the title page is not just decoration—it tells you who wrote it, why it matters, and what credentials the author brings. In this lesson, we will parse the title page of al-Ghazali's 'Mahakk al-Nazar,' a work on logic, and learn to read between the lines of scholarly honorifics and publishing details.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Title and Subject
Look at the first line: 'مُحَالُ النَّظَرِ' (Mahakk al-Nazar) meaning 'The Touchstone of Intellect.' The next line says 'في فن المنطق' (in the art of logic). This immediately tells you the book's topic and purpose—it is a criterion for distinguishing correct reasoning from fallacious.
The title itself is a clue: 'محك' means touchstone or criterion, so the book is a tool for evaluating arguments.
2
Extract the Author's Full Name
The author is listed with his full lineage: 'أبو حامد محمد بن محمد بن محمد بن أحمد الغزالي الطوسي الشافعي'. This includes his kunya (Abu Hamid), his given name (Muhammad), his father's and grandfather's names, his nisba (al-Ghazali al-Tusi al-Shafi'i) indicating his origin and madhhab. This level of detail is standard for classical works to avoid confusion with other authors.
Al-Ghazali's nisba 'al-Shafi'i' tells you he follows the Shafi'i school of fiqh, which is relevant to his legal arguments.
3
Interpret the Honorific Titles
The author is called 'الإمام المجدد' (the reviving Imam), 'حجة الإسلام والمسلمين' (the proof of Islam and Muslims), and 'زين الدين' (ornament of the religion). These titles are not arbitrary; they reflect his high scholarly rank and his role as a mujaddid (renewer) of the faith. Recognizing these titles helps you gauge the author's authority and the expected impact of the work.
The phrase 'رضي الله عنه' is a common supplication for early scholars, indicating respect and piety.
4
Note the Dates and Publisher
The birth and death years are given: 450-505 AH. This places al-Ghazali in the 5th-6th centuries AH. The bottom lines show that this edition was prepared by 'اللجنة العلمية بمركز دار المنهاج' (the scientific committee at Dar al-Minhaj Center). Understanding the publisher and critical edition is important for assessing the reliability of the text.
Modern critical editions often include a brief note about the manuscript sources used, which you can check for scholarly rigor.

Source Text

(450 - 505 AH). Honored to serve and care for it. The Scientific Committee at Dar al-Minhaj Center for Studies and Scientific Investigation. Dar al-Minhaj.
Source pages p. 4

Commentary
This passage is the title page of the book 'Mahakk al-Nazar', a work on logic by the renowned scholar Abu Hamid al-Ghazali. It begins with the book's title, which means 'The Touchstone of Intellect' or 'The Criterion of Reflection', indicating that the work is a criterion for distinguishing correct reasoning from fallacious. The phrase 'في فن المنطق' identifies it as belonging to the discipline of logic (mantiq). The author is introduced with a series of honorific titles: 'الإمام المجدد' (the reviving Imam), 'حجة الإسلام والمسلمين' (the proof of Islam and Muslims), and 'زين الدين' (ornament of the religion). His full name is given as Abu Hamid Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Ghazali al-Tusi al-Shafi'i. The mention of 'رضي الله عنه' is a supplication. His birth and death dates (450-505 AH) are provided. The final lines indicate that this edition was prepared and published by a scientific committee at Dar al-Minhaj. This front matter establishes the authority of the work and its author.

Key Takeaway
A classical title page provides essential information about the author's identity, authority, and the book's subject, which you must parse carefully before engaging with the content.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find the title page of al-Shafi'i's 'al-Risala' in a published edition. Identify the author's full name, his honorifics, and the publisher. Explain what the honorifics tell you about al-Shafi'i's standing in Islamic law.
?
Compare the title page of 'Mahakk al-Nazar' with that of al-Ghazali's 'Tahafut al-Falasifa'. What differences in honorifics or subject descriptions do you notice, and what might they indicate about the purpose of each work?

Title Page and Bibliographic Introduction to Mahakk al-Nazar
Title page and bibliographic information of Mahakk Nazar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author, title, and subject of al-Ghazali's work on logic from its title page, and explain why al-Ghazali's approach to logic is important in Islamic intellectual history.

Core Idea
Al-Ghazali's Mahakk al-Nazar is a touchstone for integrating logic into Islamic theology.

This lesson introduces the title page of Imam al-Ghazali's work on logic, Mahakk al-Nazar (The Touchstone of Inquiry). While it may seem like a simple bibliographic record, this page tells us exactly who the author is, what the book is about, and why it matters. Al-Ghazali, known as Hujjat al-Islam (The Proof of Islam), wrote this work to demonstrate how logical reasoning can serve Islamic theology. Understanding these details anchors your study of the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the title
Find the title 'محك النظر' and its translation 'The Touchstone of Inquiry'. Understand that 'Mahakk' means touchstone or criterion, implying this book is a tool for testing arguments.
The title sets the purpose of the work.
2
Analyze the author's name and titles
Read the full name: أبو حامد محمد بن محمد بن محمد بن أحمد الغزالي. Note the honorifics: الإمام المجدد (the Renewing Imam), حجة الإسلام (Proof of Islam). These indicate his high status in Islamic scholarship.
Al-Ghazali's title 'Proof of Islam' shows he is a key authority.
3
Identify the subject
The phrase 'في فن المنطق' tells us the subject is the art of logic (mantiq). This book is about logical reasoning.
Logic is the core discipline of this work.
4
Examine publication details
Note the edition: first edition 1437 AH / 2016 CE. The publisher is likely Dar al-Minhaj. This tells us the book is a modern publication, making it accessible.
5
Connect to al-Ghazali's intellectual project
Al-Ghazali wrote multiple works on logic, including Mi'yar al-'Ilm and this one. He sought to adapt Aristotelian logic for Islamic purposes. Understanding his context helps grasp the text's significance.
Al-Ghazali was a key figure in integrating logic into mainstream Islamic theology.

The work is on the subject of logic (mantiq). The date range (450-505 AH) indicates his lifespan. The edition information shows this is a modern publication by Dar al-Minhaj. The passage serves as a bibliographic introduction to the text.

Introduction to Mahakk al-Nazar Front Matter
Publisher details and copyright notice for the book

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author and title of Mahakk al-Nazar and explain the significance of front matter in an Islamic scholarly text.

Core Idea
Front matter establishes the authority and authenticity of the work.

This lesson covers the front matter of Imam al-Ghazali's Mahakk al-Nazar. While not part of the logical content, this information is crucial for understanding the book's provenance and scholarly context. Knowing the author and publisher connects you to the Islamic scholarly tradition.

Guided Path
1
Locate the author and title
Find the book title 'محك النظر' and the author 'الإمام الغزالي' in the Arabic text. This confirms the work's identity.
2
Identify the publisher and edition
Note the publisher 'دار المنهاج' and the edition 'الطبعة الأولى'. This indicates the source's reliability.
3
Understand the copyright notice
Read the copyright statement: 'لا يسمح بإعادة نشر هذا الكتاب...' This protects the publisher's rights and ensures the work's integrity.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Imam Ghazali on Logic as the Foundation of All Sciences
Quote from Imam Ghazali asserting logic as the introduction to all sciences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to articulate al-Ghazali's claim that logic is the foundation of all Islamic sciences and explain why he considers mastery of logic necessary for scholarly trustworthiness.

Core Idea
Logic is not optional for a scholar—it is the key to reliable knowledge in every Islamic science.

This passage from Imam al-Ghazali sets the tone for the entire book. He declares that logic is the introduction to all sciences (muqaddimat al-'ulum). Without it, no scholar's knowledge can be trusted. This is a strong statement that places logic at the heart of Islamic learning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and context
Recognize that this is a quote from Imam al-Ghazali, a leading scholar of the Islamic tradition. Understand that it is used as front matter in Mahakk al-Nazar to signal the author's agreement.
2
Extract the core claim
Find the phrase 'علم المنطق مقدمته العلوم كلها' (the science of logic is the introduction to all sciences). Note that 'muqaddima' means foundation or prerequisite.
3
Understand the consequence
Analyze the conditional: 'ومن لا يحيط بها فلا نثق بعلومه أصلاً' (whoever does not encompass it, we do not trust his sciences at all). This shows the necessity of logic for reliability.
4
Reflect on the implication for your studies
Consider that al-Ghazali's view makes logic a prerequisite for mastering any Islamic science, including fiqh, kalam, and tafsir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا إله إلا الله. علم المنطق، مقدمته العلوم كلها. ومن لا يحيط بها ... فلا نَثِقْ بعلومه أصلاً. الإمام الغزالي في التصفي.
There is no god but Allah. The science of logic is the introduction to all sciences. And whoever does not encompass it ... we do not trust his sciences at all. Imam al-Ghazali in al-Tashfi.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is a quotation from Imam Abu Hamid al-Ghazali (d. 505 AH/1111 CE) affirming the foundational role of logic in the Islamic sciences. It is placed as front matter in Mahakk al-Nazar, signaling the author's agreement with al-Ghazali's view. The phrase 'There is no god but Allah' is a pious opening. Then al-Ghazali states that logic ('ilm al-mantiq) is the introduction (muqaddima) to all sciences. This means that before studying any discipline—be it fiqh, kalam, tafsir, or usul—one must master logic, because logic provides the tools for sound reasoning and argumentation. He then issues a strong warning: whoever does not encompass (yuhitu biha) logic—i.e., does not fully grasp its rules—we do not trust his knowledge at all. This underscores the necessity of logic for epistemic reliability. The title 'al-Tashfi' likely refers to al-Ghazali's work 'al-Tashfi' or 'al-Tashfi fi al-Mantiq' (The Healing in Logic), though the exact title is unclear. The passage sets the tone for the entire book: logic is not optional but essential for any scholar seeking certainty.

Key Terms
علم المنطق
مقدمة العلوم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage from Imam al-Ghazali, what is the status of the science of logic?
A) It is optional for scholars of fiqh.
B) It is the introduction to all sciences and essential for trustworthy knowledge.
C) It is only relevant for logic specialists.
D) It is a Greek innovation that should be avoided.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ghazali establishes logic as the indispensable foundation for all Islamic sciences, without which no knowledge can be deemed reliable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Write a one-sentence summary of al-Ghazali's argument that logic is essential for all sciences, using your own words.
?
Explain why a jurist (faqih) would need logic to correctly derive a ruling from the Quran and hadith.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Logic as the Foundation of All Sciences
Ghazali declares logic as the necessary foundation for all sciences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain al-Ghazali's claim that logic is the muqaddima to all sciences and defend its necessity.

Core Idea
Logic is the gateway to all certain knowledge.

Imam al-Ghazali opens his work with a powerful declaration: logic is not merely one science among many—it is the indispensable introduction (muqaddima) to every field of knowledge. Without it, no discipline can be trusted. This lesson unpacks that claim and its implications for the Islamic intellectual tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim
Find the phrase 'علم المنطق، مقدمته العلوم كلها' in the Arabic. Al-Ghazali states directly that logic is the introduction or prerequisite to all sciences.
2
Understand the warning
Read the condition: 'ومن لا يحيط بها ... فلا نفر که بعلومه أصلاً'. This warns that anyone who does not fully encompass logic cannot be trusted in any science.
The OCR suggests 'نفر که' may be 'ثقة له', meaning 'no trust in him'.
3
Consider the implication
Logic is not optional or supplementary—it is mandatory for reliable knowledge. Without sound reasoning, even religious sciences like fiqh and kalam can lead to error.
4
Relate to the tradition
Later scholars like al-Taftazani refined this view but retained the primacy of logic. This quote anchors the entire logical tradition in Islamic education.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اله الا اله إلى الله علم المنطق، مقدمته العلوم كلها ومن لا يحيط بها ... فلا نفر که بعلومه أصلاً الإمام الغزالي في التصفي.
There is no god but Allah. Logic, its introduction is all sciences. And whoever does not encompass them... so no trust in his sciences at all. Imam al-Ghazali in al-Tasfi.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is a front matter quote from Imam al-Ghazali emphasizing the foundational importance of logic. The phrase 'علم المنطق، مقدمته العلوم كلها' states that logic is the introduction or prerequisite to all sciences. The following condition 'ومن لا يحيط بها ... فلا نفر که بعلومه أصلاً' warns that anyone who does not fully encompass logic cannot be trusted in his knowledge of any science. This reflects the classical Islamic view that sound reasoning is essential for attaining certainty in all disciplines, from fiqh to kalam.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Al-Ghazali's Model of Intellect and Revelation
Author praises al-Ghazali as exemplary intellect illuminated by revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between truth-seeking inquiry and polemical debate using al-Ghazali's example as a criterion.

Core Idea
The sound intellect must be illuminated by revelation to avoid monopolizing truth.

This preface sets the stage for logical inquiry by presenting al-Ghazali as the archetype of a rational investigator whose intellect is saturated with the light of divine law. The author contrasts earnest truth-seeking with the partisan polemics of his time, establishing the ethical foundation for sound reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the qualities of al-Ghazali's intellect
From the passage, list the characteristics that make al-Ghazali a model: sound intellect (العقل الرزين), saturated with the light of law (المتشبع بنور الشرع), supported by Allah, sincere, zealous for truth, loving every truth-seeker regardless of label.
2
Contrast with the practices of factions
The passage describes factions that monopolized truth, made debates a stage for controversy, filled dialogues with fallacies and doubts. Note the key differences: sincerity vs. partisanship, openness vs. monopoly.
3
Derive the methodological lesson
Al-Ghazali's approach shows that true logical inquiry requires humility and a sincere desire for truth, not victory. The tool of logic is corrupted when used to defend a predetermined position. This sets the intention (niyya) for all subsequent logical analysis.

بین یدکیسے الكتاب
نحمدك على نعمك كلّها يا وليَّ النِّعم ، ونصلي ونسلم على سيدنا محمد عبدك ونبيك سيد العرب والعجم ، وآله وصحبه هداة الأمم ، ما جالَ فكر فسوَّدَ الطرسَ القلمُ . وبعد : فلو التمس ملتمس مثالاً للعقل الرزين المتشبع بنور الشرع ، المؤيَّد من عند الله تعالى بالتوفيق والتسديد . . لرأى حجة الإسلام أُمْثولةً تروى ولا تطوى ، وصحيفة ذهبية من تاريخ الفكر الإسلامي المشرق ؛ لما حباه مولاه من خصائص أهل الكمال ، ولما انطوى عليه صدرُهُ من الإخلاص والصدق ، والغيرة على الله وأهله ، والحبّ لكل طالب حق ، ما دام يستفرغ جهده صادقاً مجتهداً . الغزالي الإمامُ الذي أعاد الحقِّ إلى نصابه حينما جلَّى أن الحق شرعة للجميع ، وأهلوه هم من تلبسوا به أياً كانت أسماؤهم ونعوتهم ، في عصر احتكرت الفرقُ والطوائف الحق لتجعله وَقْفاً عليها ، وجعلت من المناظرات العلمية مسرحاً لإثارة الجدل ، لا بحثاً عن الحقيقة ، وملأت حواراتها بالأغاليط والشبهات
Before you [?] the book. We praise You for all Your blessings, O Wali of blessings, and we send blessings and peace upon our master Muhammad, Your servant and Prophet, master of Arabs and non-Arabs, and upon his family and companions, guides of nations, as long as thought roams and the pen blackens the page. After: if someone seeks an example of the sound intellect saturated with the light of the Law, supported by Allah Almighty with success and guidance, he would see the Proof of Islam as a model to be narrated and not folded, and a golden page from the history of bright Islamic thought; because his Lord endowed him with the characteristics of the people of perfection, and because his chest contained sincerity and truthfulness, zeal for Allah and His people, and love for every seeker of truth, as long as he exerts his effort sincerely and diligently. Al-Ghazali is the Imam who restored truth to its place when he clarified that truth is a shared path for all, and its people are those who are characterized by it regardless of their names and attributes, in an age when sects and factions monopolized truth to make it a waqf for themselves, and turned scholarly debates into a stage for stirring controversy, not for searching for truth, and filled their dialogues with fallacies and doubts.
Source pages p. 12

Commentary
This passage is the preface of Mahakk al-Nazar, opening with praise of Allah and blessings on the Prophet Muhammad. It then presents a commendation of Imam al-Ghazali, referred to as 'Proof of Islam' (حجة الإسلام), as the ideal example of a rational intellect permeated by the light of divine law. The author explains that anyone seeking a model of sound reasoning supported by revelation would find it in al-Ghazali, who is described as possessing sincerity, zeal, and love for truth. The passage contrasts al-Ghazali's approach with that of his contemporaries, who turned debates into disputes and monopolized truth for their sects. Al-Ghazali is credited with re-establishing truth as a common path for all, regardless of labels. This introduction sets the tone for the work, framing it as a contribution to logical discourse guided by Islamic principles.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
The Pursuit of Truth and the Need for Logic
Author introduces the book and extols the virtue of seeking truth through sound reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain al-Ghazali's principle of accepting truth from any source and articulate why logic is necessary for distinguishing truth from falsehood.

Core Idea
Truth is universal and must be accepted regardless of the speaker; logic is the tool to uncover it.

Al-Ghazali begins his work by challenging the sectarianism of his time. He argues that truth belongs to no faction and that the intelligent person accepts truth wherever it appears. This lesson explores that principle and sets the stage for the logical tools to follow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context
Notice the author's praise of al-Ghazali and the contrast with the contemporary situation where factions monopolized truth and debates were full of fallacies.
This sets up the problem that logic will address.
2
Locate the key principle
Find the quote from al-Ghazali's 'Munqidh': 'The intelligent person knows the truth, then looks at the statement itself; if it is true, he accepts it whether its speaker is a wrongdoer or truthful.'
This is the core of the lesson: truth is independent of the speaker.
3
Understand the supporting evidence
The hadith from Mu'adh ibn Jabal: 'Accept truth from whoever comes with it, even if he is a disbeliever or a sinner.' This reinforces the principle.
This shows the principle is rooted in Islamic tradition.
4
Recognize the need for logic
Al-Ghazali notes the path to certainty is long and perils many; therefore a guide is needed. This guide is logic (mantiq), which helps extract truth from any speech.
The preface thus motivates the study of logic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نحمدك على نعمك كلّها يا وليَّ النِّعم ، ونصلي ونسلم على سيدنا محمد عبدك ونبيك سيد العرب والعجم ، وآله وصحبه هداة الأمم ، ما جالَ فكر فسوَّدَ الطرسَ القلمُ . وبعد : فلو التمس ملتمس مثالاً للعقل الرزين المتشبع بنور الشرع ، المؤيَّد من عند الله تعالى بالتوفيق والتسديد . . لرأى حجة الإسلام أُمْثولةً تروى ولا تطوى ، وصحيفة ذهبية من تاريخ الفكر الإسلامي المشرق ؛ لما حباه مولاه من خصائص أهل الكمال ، ولما انطوى عليه صدرُهُ من الإخلاص والصدق ، والغيرة على الله وأهله ، والحبّ لكل طالب حق ، ما دام يستفرغ جهده صادقاً مجتهداً . الغزالي الإمامُ الذي أعاد الحقِّ إلى نصابه حينما جلَّى أن الحق شرعة للجميع ، وأهلوه هم من تلبسوا به أياً كانت أسماؤهم ونعوتهم ، في عصر احتكرت الفرقُ والطوائف الحق لتجعله وَقْفاً عليها ، وجعلت من المناظرات العلمية مسرحاً لإثارة الجدل ، لا بحثاً عن الحقيقة ، وملأت حواراتها بالأغاليط والشبهات تحسب أنها على شيء ، وتستعين على باطلها برفع العقيرة ، مع لغة رخيصة من السب والشتيمة ، وليس وراء هذا إلا زيادة عنادِ المخالفين . فهو القائل في «منقذه » : ( فالعاقل يعرف الحق ، ثم ينظر في نفس القول ؛ فإن كان حقاً .. قبلَهُ سواء كان قائله مبطلاً أو محقاً ، بل ربما يحرص على انتزاع الحقِّ من تضاعيف كلام أهل الضلال ، عالماً بأن معدن الذهب الرغام ) ، وهذا من قول سيدنا معاذ رضي الله عنه : ( اقبلوا الحق من كل من جاء به وإن كان كافراً ، أو قال : فاجراً ) . إن الأمَّة التي لا تخاف من الحق أينما نزل وحلَّ .. هي الأمة التي تعلم أنها على حق ؛ فما كتم الحق إلا أهل الباطل ، وليس دَركُهُ بالأمر الهين ، ولذا قال الإمام في كتابنا هذا « مِحَك النظر » وهو يحدّث عن الحق واليقين : ( ولكن الطريق طويل ، والمهالك فيها كثيرة ، والمرشد عزيز، فلأجلها صار الطريق عند الأكثر مهجوراً ؛ إذ صار مجهولاً ) ، فلا عجب إذاً أن تزل قدم بعد ثبوتها ، وأن ترى أعلاماً غلبت عليهم آفة العصر المتمثلة في تشويه الحقائق وتزيين الأباطيل ، فاندفعت ألسنتهم تحدّث بغير منطق
We praise You for all Your blessings, O Guardian of blessings, and we pray and send peace upon our master Muhammad, Your servant and Prophet, the master of Arabs and non-Arabs, and upon his family and companions, the guides of nations, as long as thought roams and the pen blackens the page. Thereafter: If someone sought an example of a sound intellect saturated with the light of the Law, supported by God Almighty with success and guidance, he would see the Proof of Islam (al-Ghazali) as an exemplar to be narrated and not folded, a golden page from the radiant history of Islamic thought; because his Lord bestowed upon him the characteristics of the people of perfection, and because his chest contained sincerity and truthfulness, zeal for God and His people, and love for every seeker of truth, as long as he exhausts his effort sincerely and diligently. Al-Ghazali is the Imam who restored truth to its proper place when he made clear that truth is a common law for all, and its people are those who embody it regardless of their names and attributes, in an era when sects and factions monopolized truth to make it an endowment for themselves, and turned scholarly debates into a stage for stirring up controversy, not a search for truth, and filled their dialogues with fallacies and doubts, thinking they are upon something, and they relied for their falsehood on raising voices, with cheap language of insults and abuse, behind which there is nothing but increased stubbornness of opponents. So he said in his 'Munqidh': 'The intelligent person knows the truth, then looks at the statement itself; if it is true, he accepts it whether its speaker is a wrongdoer or truthful. Rather, he may be keen to extract truth from the folds of the speech of the people of misguidance, knowing that the gold mine is in the dust.' And this is from the saying of our master Mu'adh, may God be pleased with him: 'Accept truth from whoever comes with it, even if he is a disbeliever, or he said: a sinful person.' Indeed, a nation that does not fear truth wherever it descends and settles is a nation that knows it is upon truth; for none conceals truth except the people of falsehood, and attaining it is not an easy matter. Hence the Imam said in this book of ours, 'Mahakk al-Nazar', while speaking about truth and certainty: 'But the path is long, the perils in it are many, and the guide is scarce; therefore the path has become for most people deserted because it has become unknown.' So it is no wonder that a foot slips after it was firm, and that you see prominent figures overcome by the affliction of the age manifested in distorting truths and beautifying falsehoods, so their tongues rush to speak without logic.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is the preface to al-Ghazali's 'Mahakk al-Nazar'. The author begins with praise of God and blessings upon the Prophet, then introduces the subject by extolling the virtues of al-Ghazali, whom he presents as the model of a sound intellect guided by divine law. He describes al-Ghazali as the one who restored truth to its proper place, emphasizing that truth is a common law for all and that its adherents are those who embody it, regardless of their labels. The author contrasts this with the contemporary situation where factions monopolized truth and turned debates into contentious arguments filled with fallacies and insults. He then quotes al-Ghazali's own words from 'al-Munqidh min al-Dalal' that an intelligent person accepts truth from anyone, even from the people of misguidance, likening truth to gold that can be extracted from dust. He also cites a hadith from Mu'adh ibn Jabal to accept truth even from a disbeliever or sinner. The preface concludes with the author quoting al-Ghazali's statement about the difficulty of the path to certainty: the way is long, perils many, and guides scarce, so most people abandon it out of ignorance. This sets up the need for the logical principles that al-Ghazali will present in the book, as a tool for discerning truth from falsehood.

الحق
منطق

Key Takeaway
Truth is universal and must be sought through sound reasoning; logic serves as the tool to extract it from any source, regardless of the speaker's identity.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

The Definition and Purpose of Logic
Definition of logic as an instrument of certainty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three components of logic as defined in Mahakk al-Nazar and explain how each safeguards the mind.

Core Idea
Logic is the instrument that guards the intellect from error and unveils certainty.

After lamenting the prevalence of falsehood, the editor asks the pivotal question: What is logic? His answer is not a dry definition but a functional description revealing logic's essential role in the Islamic intellectual tradition. The passage presents three complementary characterizations that together define logic's purpose.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition
Find the sentence beginning with 'وما المنطق؟' and read the entire answer. The editor provides three descriptions separated by 'أو'.
2
Identify the three characterizations
List them: (1) instrument that safeguards the mind from error, (2) work of the sound intellect, (3) lifting the veil of illusion and conjecture to see certainty.
Each highlights a different facet of logic.
3
Analyze the term 'ālah'
Note that logic is called an 'instrument' (آلة), implying it is a tool to be used, not an end in itself. The word 'iṣmah (safeguard) is a strong term, often used for prophetic infallibility.
This metaphorical usage elevates logic's protective function.
4
Connect to the goal
The ultimate aim is 'pure gold of certainty' (نضار اليقين). Logic achieves this by removing obstacles (illusion and conjecture) that block clear reasoning.

لا شك أن أقدار الله لا تغالب ، بل الله غالب على أمره ، ولكننا نجد في « المِحَك ) الذي بين أيدينا وفي ( المعيار » أيضاً احتراماً كبيراً لقانون الأسباب والمسببات ، حتى إنه قال : ( يجوز أن يفرض في المحل أمور تدفع المسبَّبَ ، ولا يدل ذلك على بطلان السببية ) (۱) ، وقال : ( من أخبر بأن ولده حزّتْ رقبته .. لم يشك في موته ، وليس في العقلاء من يشك فيه ) (٢) ، فلا بدَّ من

If he does not wake up from his heedlessness and arise from his slumber. There is no doubt that the decrees of Allah cannot be overcome, rather Allah is dominant over His command, but we find in 'al-Mihakk' that is before us and in 'al-Mi'yar' also great respect for the law of causes and effects, until he said: 'It is possible to assume in a situation matters that prevent the effect, and that does not indicate the invalidity of causality.' And he said: 'Whoever is informed that his son's neck was cut, he does not doubt his death, and there is no sane person who doubts it.' So it is necessary to...
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage is an introductory commentary by the editor of 'Mahakk al-Nazar', setting the stage for the importance of logic and truth. It opens by criticizing those who use falsehood with loudness and abuse, then quotes al-Ghazali's 'al-Munqidh min al-Dalal' emphasizing that the wise person accepts truth regardless of its source, even from the speech of misguided people, because truth is precious like gold in dust. Then it cites the companion Mu'adh ibn Jabal (may Allah be pleased with him) instructing to accept truth from anyone, even a disbeliever or sinner. The editor then commends the Muslim nation that does not fear truth, as only the people of falsehood conceal it. He quotes al-Ghazali from 'Mahakk al-Nazar' describing the path to truth as long, full of dangers, with rare guides, leading most people to abandon it out of ignorance. Then he turns to the definition of logic: it is the instrument that safeguards the mind from error, the work of sound reason, lifting the veil of illusion and conjecture to see pure certainty. This definition highlights logic's role as a protective tool. The editor then laments current times where deliberate absence of reason leads people to be led by deceivers. Finally, he addresses the causal principle: despite Allah's absolute power, the book respects the law of cause and effect. Al-Ghazali explains that assuming obstacles that prevent an effect does not negate causality, just as being informed of a beheading leaves no doubt of death among sane people. This demonstrates that causality is a reliable natural law.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate

Causality and the Law of Cause and Effect
Defense of causality against the objection of preventive factors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain al-Ghazali's position on causality as presented in Mahakk al-Nazar and argue why assuming preventive factors does not invalidate causal laws.

Core Idea
Al-Ghazali affirms causality: obstacles to an effect do not negate the causal link itself.

After defining logic, the editor turns to a foundational principle: causality. He quotes al-Ghazali's Mahakk al-Nazar to defend the law of cause and effect against the objection that occasional preventive factors might break it. This shows that logic and causality are intertwined in the Islamic worldview.

Guided Path
1
Find the causal claim
Locate the sentence beginning with 'يجوز أن يفرض في المحل أمور تدفع المسبب'. This is the core statement on causality.
2
Identify the objection
The potential challenge is: if an effect does not occur despite the presence of the cause, might causality be invalid?
This objection arises from occasionalist thought.
3
Understand al-Ghazali's response
He says that assuming matters that prevent the effect does not indicate the invalidity of causality. The causal link remains intact; prevention is a separate issue.
This preserves causal regularity while acknowledging God's power to intervene.
4
Examine the example
The beheading example: no sane person doubts death after a beheading. This shows immediate certainty about a cause-effect relationship.
This example grounds causality in common human experience.
5
Connect to logic
The principle of causality is itself a rational tool used in arguments. It underpins analogical reasoning (qiyas) in fiqh and theological proofs.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
What is Logic and Why Must We Learn It?
Author defines logic and argues for its necessity in combating intellectual decay.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to articulate the definition of logic according to al-Ghazali and explain its necessity for intellectual integrity in Islamic sciences.

Core Idea
Logic is the shield of the intellect against error and the key to certain knowledge.

In this opening passage, the author presents logic not as a foreign discipline but as an essential tool for every seeker of truth. He defines it in three complementary ways and diagnoses the crisis of intellectual absence that afflicts even scholars. Understanding why logic is necessary prepares you to appreciate the rest of the book and its application in Islamic sciences like usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three definitions of logic
In the first sentence, the author gives three characterizations: an instrument that safeguards thought from error, the work of the rational mind, and the removal of the veil of illusion and conjecture to attain certainty. Note how they are complementary: the first emphasizes protection, the second active thinking, the third purification.
These definitions align with the standard Islamic logical tradition.
2
Analyze the author's critique of the contemporary crisis
The author laments the 'deliberate absence of intellect' and how even people of rank are led by deception. He links this to the neglect of logic. Identify the key symptoms: blind following, inability to doubt media, and the dominance of illusion.
The crisis is described as a spiritual and intellectual illness.
3
Connect logic to the law of causation
The author references al-Ghazali's al-Mihakk and al-Mi'yar to show that logical reasoning respects cause and effect. He gives examples: even if a cause can be blocked, it does not negate causation; a reported decapitation leads to certainty of death.
This shows that logic is grounded in reality and common sense.
4
Recognize the role of logic in Islamic sciences
The author states that al-Ghazali placed this logical treatise as an introduction to his major work on usul al-fiqh, al-Mustasfa. Logic is the 'truthful scale' for every seeker of truth, especially in deriving legal rulings.
Logic is not optional but foundational for sound reasoning in Islam.

وما من شكّ أن العقل المنطقي الرتيب يفنّدُ ويدحض أوهام هذه البدائل المبهرجة ، ويعلم أنها عماليق من ورق ، وأنها لا يمكنها أن تخرق أسوار البرهان ، ولكن ليس بهين صناعة مثل هذا العقل .

What is logic? It is but the instrument that safeguards thought from error, or say: the work of the rational mind, or the removal of the veil of illusion and conjecture to see the pure gold of certainty.

► There is no doubt that the decrees of Allah cannot be overcome, rather Allah prevails in His affair, but we find in "al-Mihakk" before us and in "al-Mi'yar" as well great respect for the law of causes and effects, to the point that he said: "It is permissible to suppose in the locality things that repel the effect, and that does not indicate the invalidity of causation." And he said: "Whoever is told that his son's neck was cut off... does not doubt his death, and there is no rational person who doubts it." So it is necessary to take a serious stance in light of what is happening, especially with the scarcity of authorities which is the great calamity, and the exhaustion of others' efforts in creating dominant authorities that have entered the small house and the great scientific institution. So who among us today can deny before the masses the events of the television and doubt them?

There is no doubt that the steady logical mind refutes and dispels the illusions of these flashy alternatives, and knows that they are paper giants, and that they cannot breach the walls of demonstration, but creating such a mind is not easy.

And "al-Mihakk" is a logical piece, despite its brevity, comprehensive and of great benefit, such that Imam al-Ghazali approved it as an introduction to his great usul book "al-Mustasfa", and indeed he referred to it in several of his works of various content. This attention was not arbitrary or incidental without purpose and noble intention; for refined, abstract, concise logic is a truthful scale incumbent upon every seeker of truth and caller to it.

For all this, attention came from Dar al-Minhaj in its publication, and we urge those in charge of educational institutions at all levels, and the people of knowledge who are at the peak of scholarly chains... to
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage serves as an introduction to the book Mahakk al-Nazar. The author begins by defining logic (al-mantiq) in three complementary ways: as the instrument that safeguards the intellect from error, as the operation of the rational mind, and as the removal of the veil of illusion and conjecture to attain certainty. He then laments the contemporary crisis of intellectual absence, where even scholars are led astray by deception. He praises the works of al-Ghazali, particularly al-Mihakk and al-Mi'yar, for their respect for causation and their logical rigor. The author argues that only a trained logical mind can refute falsehoods and uphold demonstration (burhan). He declares that this book is a concise but comprehensive logical treatise that al-Ghazali himself placed as an introduction to his usul al-fiqh work al-Mustasfa. The passage concludes with a call to educational institutions to revive the study of logic, as it is a truthful scale for every seeker of truth.

Key Terms
المنطق
البرهان
الوهم

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It provides emotional comfort
B) It safeguards thought from error
C) It replaces revelation
D) It is only for philosophers

Key Takeaway
Logic is the instrument that protects the mind from error and is essential for sound reasoning in Islamic sciences, as exemplified by al-Ghazali's use of it in usul al-fiqh.

The Purpose of Logic: A Scale for Truth
Editorial preface defending logic as the essential instrument of truth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the editor's argument for the importance of logic and explain how Al-Miḥak serves as a foundational logical text.

Core Idea
Logic is the purified scale that refutes illusions and upholds demonstration.

In this editorial preface, the publisher Dar al-Minhaj makes a compelling case for the study of logic. They argue that in an age of unreliable references and flashy deceptions, only a rigorous logical mind can distinguish truth from falsehood. The preface highlights al-Ghazali's endorsement of the concise logical work 'Al-Miḥak' as the key to building such a mind.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
The editor describes the scarcity of reliable references and the prevalence of flashy alternatives. What is the 'great calamity'?
Look for the phrase 'عزة المرجعيات التي هي المصيبة الكبرى'.
2
Find the solution proposed
What does the editor say is needed to refute illusions?
The answer is 'العقل المنطقي الرتيب' (the steady logical mind).
3
Examine the evidence
What role does al-Ghazali's Al-Miḥak play?
Al-Ghazali approved it as an introduction to Al-Mustasfa and referred to it in other works.
4
Extract the definition of logic
How does the editor describe logic?
He calls it 'المنطق المحرر المجرد الوجيز ميزان صادق' (purified, abstract, concise true scale).
5
Understand the call to action
What does the editor urge educational institutions to do?
To make Al-Miḥak and similar works a mandatory station for learning.

Taking a serious stance in light of what is happening, especially with the scarcity of reliable references – which is the great calamity – and the exhaustion of others' efforts in manufacturing dominant references that have entered the small house and the great scientific institution. Who among us today can deny before the masses the events on screen and cast doubt on them? There is no doubt that the steady logical mind refutes and demolishes the illusions of these flashy alternatives, and knows that they are paper giants, and that they cannot breach the walls of demonstration (burhan). But producing such a mind is not easy. And 'Al-Miḥak' is a logical piece, despite its subtlety, comprehensive and of great benefit, such that Imam al-Ghazali approved it as an introduction to his great usuli book 'Al-Mustasfa', and even referred to it in a number of his works of diverse subjects. This attention was not arbitrary or casual without a purpose and noble intention. For purified, abstract, concise logic is a true scale incumbent upon every seeker of truth and caller to it. For all this, attention was given by Dar al-Minhaj in publishing it. And we call upon those in charge of educational institutions at all levels, and upon the people of knowledge who are at the peak of scholarly chains, to make (Al-Miḥak) and its like a station that must be stopped at and supplied from, so that the scholar of the future is confident in his knowledge, not accepting hesitation in certainty, nor accepting certainty in places of conjecture. May Allah be with us and with every sincere and truthful one. From Him, glorified is He, is assistance and support. Praise be to Allah, Lord of the worlds. Friday, 1 Safar 1437 AH, corresponding to 13 November 2015 AD. Next.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is an editorial preface by the publisher, Dar al-Minhaj, introducing the book 'Al-Miḥak' and emphasizing the importance of logic. The author argues that in an age of unreliable references and flashy but false alternatives, the logical mind is essential to refute illusions and uphold demonstration (burhan). He praises al-Ghazali's 'Al-Miḥak' as a concise yet comprehensive logical work that al-Ghazali himself used as an introduction to his major work in usul al-fiqh, 'Al-Mustasfa'. The editor asserts that purified, abstract logic is a true scale for every seeker of truth. He then calls upon educational institutions and scholars to make this book a mandatory stop in learning, so that future scholars are confident in their knowledge, distinguishing between certainty and conjecture. The preface ends with a date and a prayer.

Al-Mihakk as a Touchstone for Certainty
Editor describes the book as a station for certainty and caution against false certainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to articulate the role of al-Mihakk as a tool for distinguishing genuine certainty from false certainty in Islamic logical inquiry.

Core Idea
Al-Mihakk trains the scholar to stand firm in certainty and reject certainty in conjecture.

This passage, from the front matter of al-Mihakk, sets the stage for the entire work. It describes the book as a necessary station (maḥaṭṭa) for the seeker of knowledge, where he must pause and equip himself. The goal is to produce a scholar who is confident in his certain knowledge without wavering, yet humble enough not to claim certainty where only conjecture (ẓann) exists. Let's unpack this powerful vision.

Guided Path
1
Identify the station metaphor
Notice that the book is called a 'station' (maḥaṭṭa). In Islamic intellectual travel, a station is a place to stop and provision. What is the traveler supposed to take from this station?
The 'provision' is the ability to distinguish certainty from doubt.
2
Extract the dual caution
The text warns against two opposite errors: accepting hesitation in certainty (i.e., doubting certain matters) and accepting certainty in places of conjecture (i.e., being overconfident in weak evidence). Identify these two in the Arabic.
This is a key epistemic balance taught in Islamic logic.
3
Connect to the purpose of logical tools
Al-Mihakk, meaning 'touchstone', is a tool to test arguments. How does this passage frame the ultimate purpose of such logical tools? They are not mere theoretical exercises but to produce scholars confident in their knowledge.
This reframes logic as a practical instrument for sound scholarship.

This passage is a front matter statement by the editor, likely describing the purpose of the book 'al-Mihakk' (The Touchstone). The book is presented as an essential station for the seeker of knowledge, where he must pause and take provisions. The aim is to produce a scholar who is confident in his certain knowledge and does not waver in certainty, nor does he claim certainty in matters that are merely conjectural. The passage ends with a prayer for divine assistance.

Al-Ghazali's Authority and His Logical Legacy
Biography of al-Ghazali detailing his death, works, and scholarly praise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical details of Imam al-Ghazali and explain how his scholarly authority underpins the logical method in his book Mahakk al-Nazar.

Core Idea
Al-Ghazali's unmatched scholarship gives his logical works unmatched authority.

Imam al-Ghazali is not just any author; his biography shows a life devoted to knowledge, immense output, and universal scholarly acclaim. Understanding his background helps us appreciate why his logical treatise Mahakk al-Nazar carries weight in the Islamic tradition. This lesson guides you through the biographical evidence that establishes al-Ghazali as a reliable authority.

Guided Path
1
Trace his final years
Find where he died and how he spent his time after leaving formal teaching. The text says he divided his time between Quran recitation, teaching, advice, and guidance until death in Tus, 505 AH.
This shows his devotion remained strong till the end.
2
Quantify his scholarly output
Note the statement about his books being counted and distributed over his lifetime: four quires per day. That is an extraordinary level of productivity.
This output is presented as a divine gift.
3
Identify his logical works
From the list of works, pick those related to logic: 'Mihakk al-Nazar' (the present book), 'Mi'yar al-'Ilm', 'al-Qistas al-Mustaqim'. These show his focus on logic.
These works form part of his broader methodology.
4
Analyse the scholarly testimonies
Read the five praises from al-Juwayni, Ibn 'Asakir, Ibn al-Najjar, al-Dhahabi, and Ibn al-Subki. They attest to his mastery in jurisprudence, theology, and sciences.
The consensus among these authorities establishes his rank.
5
Connect authority to the book
Reflect: why would a logical work by such a figure be considered a trusted reference? Because his credentials ensure the reasoning is sound and rooted in the Islamic tradition.
This is why the front matter is instructive.

Then he left the school, and returned to his home, dividing his time between reciting the Quran, teaching and giving benefit, advice and guidance, until death came to him in Tus in the year 505 AH. May God be pleased with him. Imam al-Ghazali, may God be pleased with him, left behind famous works that had not been preceded; whoever ponders them knows his virtue and rank in the sciences of knowledge. It has been said: 'The books of al-Ghazali that he authored were counted and distributed over his lifetime; each day was allotted four quires (of writing), and that is the bounty of God which He gives to whom He wills.' Some of his beneficial works include: 'Ihya' 'Ulum al-Din', 'al-Iqtisad fi al-I'tiqad', 'Maqasid al-Falasifa', 'Bidayat al-Hidaya', 'Tahafut al-Falasifa', 'al-Munqidh min al-Dalal', and 'Mihakk al-Nazar' which is this our book. Also 'Mi'yar al-'Ilm', 'al-Qistas al-Mustaqim', 'al-Mankhul', 'al-Mustasfa', 'al-Basit', 'al-Wasit', 'al-Wajiz', 'al-Khulasa', and 'Iljam al-'Awamm'. And among the praises of scholars concerning him: His teacher Imam al-Juwayni said: 'Al-Ghazali is an overwhelming sea.' Al-Hafiz Ibn 'Asakir said: 'He was an imam in the science of jurisprudence, both school and disagreement, and in the principles of religions.' Al-Hafiz Ibn al-Najjar said: 'The imam of jurists absolutely, the rabbani of the nation by consensus, and the mujtahid of his time.' Al-Hafiz al-Dhahabi said: 'The shaykh, the imam, the sea, the Proof of Islam, the wonder of the age.' Imam Ibn al-Subki said: 'The Proof of Islam, the clear path of religion by which one reaches the abode of peace, the gatherer of the scattered sciences, the outstanding one in transmitted and understood knowledge.' May God be pleased with him, honor his resting place, and benefit through his sciences; indeed He is the best of those asked.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is a biographical sketch of Imam al-Ghazali, the author of Mahakk al-Nazar. It begins by describing his final years: he left formal teaching and returned home, devoting his time to Quran recitation, teaching, and guidance until his death in Tus in 505 AH. The text then highlights his immense scholarly output, noting that he produced an average of four quires (karraris) of writing each day of his adult life—a mark of divine favor. A list of his major works follows, including his magnum opus Ihya' 'Ulum al-Din, philosophical critiques like Tahafut al-Falasifa, and logical works such as Mi'yar al-'Ilm, al-Qistas al-Mustaqim, and the present book, Mahakk al-Nazar. The passage concludes with glowing testimonies from five prominent scholars: his teacher al-Juwayni (who called him an overwhelming sea), Ibn 'Asakir, Ibn al-Najjar, al-Dhahabi, and Ibn al-Subki—all attesting to his mastery of jurisprudence, theology, and the sciences. This introduction establishes the authority of the author before delving into the logical content of the book.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate

Al-Ghazali's Conception of Logic and Purpose of al-Mihakk
Author explains his relationship with earlier logicians and the reasons for writing this book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between al-Ghazali's view of logic as an innate science and the technical terminology of the philosophers, and identify the dual motives for writing al-Mihakk.

Core Idea
Logic is not Greek jargon but an innate tool of sound minds—al-Ghazali wrote al-Mihakk to reclaim it.

In this opening passage, al-Ghazali sets the stage for his logical work by clarifying his stance on the nature of logic and its place in Islamic scholarship. He challenges the notion that he simply followed al-Farabi and Ibn Sina, and instead presents logic as a universal science inherent in sound intellects. Understanding his motives for writing al-Mihakk—both as a response to the monopolization of logic and as a student-driven demand for a safeguard against error—will help you appreciate the purpose and structure of the book.

Guided Path
1
Identify al-Ghazali's claim about the source of logic
Find the sentence where al-Ghazali states that he did not simply follow al-Farabi and Ibn Sina, but rather considered logic as a fixed science in the core of sound minds, abstracted from technical terms.
This distinguishes his approach from the Greek-influenced tradition.
2
Analyze his relationship with the philosophers
Note how he defends his harsh judgment in al-Munqidh, clarifying that the takfir was aimed at those who mocked the Shari'a, not initially at the philosophers themselves. The philosophers were only an example.
This nuance is often misunderstood.
3
Trace the distinction between logicians' terminology and Islamic scholars' usage
Al-Ghazali points out that Islamic jurists, usuliyyun, and mutakallimun wrote on logic under titles like Kitab al-Jadal and al-Nazar, which is logic itself. The philosophers turned it into a specialized jargon.
This shows that logic was already present in Islamic sciences.
4
Extract the dual motives for writing al-Mihakk
Identify the two motives: (1) the necessity of taking up logic due to its monopolization by some and the difficulty of studying it; (2) the insistence of students for a book that protects against error and provides a scale for thought.
The book aims to make logic accessible and rigorous.
5
Reflect on the significance of the title
Consider the meaning of 'al-Mihakk' (the touchstone) as a measure for thought, based on the root h-k (to test). This ties to the protective and evaluative purpose of the book.
The title encapsulates the book's function.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب محک النظر. ثقة عظيمة كان يمتلكها الإمام الغزالي باستيلائه على ناصية علم المنطق، ذاك العلم الذي لم يترسم خطاه ابتداء من كتب الشيخين الفارابي وابن سينا كما يعتقد البعض، وإن كنا على شبه يقين بوقوفه وتأمله الطويل في كتبهما أو كتب الشيخ الرئيس على الأقل، إذ إطلاق الحكم القاسي في حقهما في «منقذه» مع ديانته وصيانته لا يمكن أن يأتي بمجرد أحاديث أخبار واهية، أو قراءة كلمات عجلة. فإن لم يكن المنطق من كتب الشيخين، فمن أين جاء به الإمام؟ من يطالع الكتب المنطقية التي ورثها الإمام حجة الإسلام يلحظ أنه يميل إلى جعل علم المنطق بمعانيه المجردة عن الاصطلاحات والوضع علما ثابتا في صميم العقول السليمة. ولا بد هنا من التنبيه إلى أن أصل هذا الحكم (وهو الكفر والزندقة) لم يتسلط عليهما ابتداء، بل إنما أطلقه الإمام على الذين سخروا في باطنهم من الشريعة وتجملوا بها خوفا من غضب العامة وما برروا لأنفسهم من ترهات، وإنما ذكرهما كمثال، وليس المثال المسوق كشاهد بقوة الحكم وبيان علته؛ إذ يقتضي المثال الصحة، وعلى فرض صحة هذا المثال لا يمكن الوقوف عند قرار الإمام في ذلك؛ إذ جملة من محقي «السنوسية» خالفوا فيه، ومالوا إلى التماس الأعذار. الراشدة، وهي في غنية عنه، ولكن الناطقية عند الإنسان لا تنفتح عن مباني تحمل هذه المعاني؛ لتدور عجلة التعليم، وتلحق العقول القاصرة بالباصرة. وقد قام أئمة الإسلام من الفقهاء المجتهدين ومن لحق بركبهم من الأصوليين والمتكلمين بتدوين أبواب في كتبهم تحت عنوانات ككتاب الجدل، والنظر، ومدارك العقول إلى آخره، مادة هذه الأبواب إنما هي المنطق بعينه، ولكن أبى الفلاسفة الإسلاميون إلا أن يهولوا الأمر بتحويل هذا إلى مصطلح المنطق. ومع أنه لا مشاحة في الاصطلاح، ولكن على ألا يكون هذا الاصطلاح مجرد تميز يراد به لفت الأنظار واستصغار النظار. إذا؛ ضرورة الأخذ بهذا العلم، ومحاولة التسلط عليه واحتكاره من قبل بعض من يهتم لأن يكون متبوعا لا تابعا وإن كان على غير هدى، وهجرهم للمصطلحات الدائرة فيه، ووعورة القراءة والدرس بعلم المنطق، كل هذا كان داعية حقيقية لتدوين «المحك». أما الداعية الأخرى، فهي إلحاح من بعض طلبة الإمام في إخراج كتاب يكون عصمة عن مكامن الغلط، وإيجاد ميزان للفكر والاعتبار. تأمل في اسم الكتاب. يقول العلامة ابن فارس في «مقاييس اللغة» (حك): (الحاء
Kitab Mihakk al-Nazar. A great confidence that Imam al-Ghazali possessed by seizing the forefront of the science of logic, that science which he did not initially follow the footsteps of from the books of the two shaykhs al-Farabi and Ibn Sina as some think, although we are almost certain of his standing and long reflection on their books or at least the books of the Chief Master (Ibn Sina), since issuing a harsh judgment against them in 'al-Munqidh' with his religiosity and integrity cannot come from mere weak reports or hasty reading. So if logic was not from the books of the two shaykhs, then from where did the Imam bring it? Whoever examines the logical books inherited by the Imam, the Proof of Islam, notices that he tends to make the science of logic with its meanings abstracted from technical terms and conventions a fixed science in the core of sound intellects. Here it is necessary to note that the origin of this judgment (which is disbelief and heresy) was not initially directed at them, but rather the Imam released it upon those who inwardly mocked the Shari'a and adorned themselves with it out of fear of the public's anger and the nonsense they justified to themselves. He only mentioned them as an example, and the example advanced is not a witness to the strength of the judgment and explanation of its cause; since the example requires validity, and on the assumption of the validity of this example, one cannot stop at the Imam's decision in that matter; since a group of researchers of the Sanusiyya opposed him in it and inclined to seek excuses. The mature (minds) are independent of it, but the rational faculty in man does not open without principles that bear these meanings, so that the wheel of teaching turns and the deficient intellects catch up with the discerning. And the imams of Islam from the mujtahid jurists and those who followed their path among the usuliyyun and mutakallimun have compiled sections in their books under titles like Kitab al-Jadal, al-Nazar, Madarik al-Uqul, etc. The material of these sections is logic itself, but the Islamic philosophers insisted on exaggerating the matter by converting this into the terminology of logic. And although there is no dispute about terminology, it should not be a mere distinction intended to attract attention and belittle the viewers. So, the necessity of taking up this science, and the attempt to dominate and monopolize it by some who care to be followed rather than follower even if not guided, and their abandonment of the terms current in it, and the difficulty of reading and studying the science of logic – all this was a real motive for writing 'al-Mihakk'. As for the other motive, it is the insistence of some of the Imam's students to produce a book that would be a protection against the pitfalls of error and provide a scale for thought and consideration. Reflection on the name of the book. Says the scholar Ibn Faris in 'Maqayis al-Lugha' (H-k): 'al-Ha'...
Source pages p. 22

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter introduction that explains the background, motivation, and purpose of the book 'Mihakk al-Nazar'. The author begins by asserting al-Ghazali's mastery of logic, noting that he did not simply follow al-Farabi and Ibn Sina as commonly thought, but rather engaged deeply with their works. The harsh judgment against them in 'al-Munqidh' is defended as not being based on flimsy reports or hasty reading. The author emphasizes that al-Ghazali considered logic as a science inherent in sound minds, abstracted from technical jargon. Then a critical clarification is made: al-Ghazali's declaration of disbelief and heresy (takfir) was not initially directed at the philosophers but at those who mocked the Shari'a; the philosophers were only mentioned as an example. This example is not a proof of the ruling's strength. The author notes that some researchers of the Sanusiyya opposed al-Ghazali's decision and sought excuses for the philosophers. The passage continues that the rational faculty needs principles, and Islamic scholars (jurists, usuliyyun, mutakallimun) have written on logic under titles like 'al-Jadal' and 'al-Nazar', which is essentially logic. The Islamic philosophers, however, turned it into a specialized terminology, which should not be a mere means of drawing attention. The author then gives the dual motives for writing 'al-Mihakk': the necessity of logic and its monopolization by some, and the insistence of students for a book that safeguards against error and serves as a measure for thought. Finally, the author begins a reflection on the name of the book, citing Ibn Faris's dictionary on the root 'h-k' (to test, to examine), which is cut off.

The Necessity of Logic and Motivation for al-Mihakk
Author explains the need for logic and cites two motivations for writing this book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish al-Ghazali's position on logic from the philosophers' position and identify the two motivations for writing al-Mihakk.

Core Idea
Al-Ghazali wrote al-Mihakk to free logic from philosophers' monopoly and provide a safeguard against error.

In this opening passage, al-Ghazali clarifies that logic is not an alien discipline but the very substance of Islamic dialectic and legal theory. He laments that the philosophers have made logic a difficult and exclusive science. This lesson will help you understand his motivations for writing al-Mihakk and his attitude towards logic as a tool.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two groups mentioned
Al-Ghazali contrasts the Islamic scholars (jurists, usuliyyun, mutakallimun) who used logical topics under different titles with the Islamic philosophers who turned logic into a monopolized terminology.
Notice that the scholars integrated logic without naming it, while the philosophers emphasized the term 'logic'.
2
Extract al-Ghazali's criticism of philosophers
He accuses the philosophers of magnifying the matter, using terminology to attract attention and belittle others, and monopolizing the science.
Al-Ghazali does not reject logic itself, only the attitude of its practitioners.
3
Identify the two motivations
First motivation: the necessity of logic combined with the philosophers' monopolization and the difficulty of studying it. Second motivation: the insistence of al-Ghazali's students for a book that protects from error and provides a criterion.
Both motivations are explicitly stated at the end of the passage.
4
Understand the significance of the title 'al-Mihakk'
The title means 'touchstone', a tool to test gold. Al-Ghazali uses this metaphor to indicate that his book is a criterion for distinguishing truth from falsehood.
This connects to the second motivation: a criterion for thought and consideration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الراشدة ، وهي في غُنْية عنه ، ولكنَّ الناطقية عند الإنسان لا تنفتُ عن مباني تحمل هذه المعاني ؛ لتدور عجلة التعليم ، وتلحق العقول القاصرة بالباصرة . وقد قام أئمة الإسلام ؛ من الفقهاء المجتهدين ، ومن لحق بركبهم من الأصوليين والمتكلمين .. بتدوين أبواب في كتبهم تحت عنوانات ؛ ككتاب الجدل ، والنظر ، ومدارك العقول إلى آخره ، مادَّةُ هذه الأبواب إنما هي المنطق بعينه ، ولكن أبى الفلاسفة الإسلاميون إلا أن يُهَوّلوا الأمر بتحويل هذا إلى مصطلح المنطق ومع أنه لا مشاحة في الاصطلاح ، ولكن على ألا يكون هذا الاصطلاح مجرَّدَ تميز يُراد به لفتُ الأنظار . واستصغار النظار . إذاً ؛ ضرورة الأخذ بهذا العلم، ومحاولة التسلط عليه واحتكاره من قبل بعض مَنْ يهتمُّ لأن يكون متبوعاً لا تابعاً وإن كان على غير هدى ، وهجرهم للمصطلحات الدائرة فيه ، ووعورة القراءة والدرس بعلم المنطق .. كلُّ هذا كان داعيةً حقيقية لتدوين ( المِحَك ) ، أما الداعية الأخرى .. فهي إلحاح من بعض طلبة الإمام في إخراج كتاب يكون عصمة عن مكامن الغلط ، وإيجاد میزان للفكر والاعتبار .
Sound opinion is in no need of it, but the rational faculty in man does not emerge from foundations that carry these meanings, so that the wheel of education turns and deficient intellects catch up with the penetrating ones. The imams of Islam—from the mujtahid jurists and those who followed their path among the uṣūliyyūn and mutakallimūn—compiled chapters in their books under titles such as ‘Book of Dialectic’, ‘Discourse’, and ‘Perceptions of the Intellect’, etc. The substance of these chapters is precisely logic. But the Islamic philosophers insisted on magnifying the matter by transforming this into the terminology of logic. And although there is no quarrel over terminology, it should not be such that this terminology is merely a distinction intended to attract attention and belittle the learned. Therefore, the necessity of adopting this science, and the attempt to dominate and monopolize it by some of those who care to be followed rather than a follower, even if on a misguided path, and their abandonment of the prevalent terms, and the difficulty of reading and studying logic—all of this was a genuine motivation for compiling al-Miḥakk. As for the other motivation, it is the insistence of some students of the Imam to produce a book that would be a safeguard against pitfalls and a criterion for thought and consideration.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is an introduction by Imam al-Ghazali explaining the reasons for writing his book al-Mihakk. He begins by stating that although sound opinion is independent, the human rational faculty requires logical foundations to educate and elevate deficient intellects. He acknowledges that Islamic scholars (jurists, usuliyyun, mutakallimun) have already dealt with logical topics in their works under different names like 'Book of Dialectic' and 'Discourse', and that the substance of those chapters is logic itself. However, he criticizes the Islamic philosophers for turning this into a specialized terminology to monopolize and intimidate, calling it a mere distinction to attract attention and belittle others. Al-Ghazali then identifies two motivations for writing al-Mihakk: first, the necessity of logic coupled with the philosophers' monopolization and the difficulty of studying it; second, the request from his students for a book that protects from error and provides a criterion for thought and consideration.

Key Terms
المنطق (al-mantiq): In this passage, al-Ghazali refers to logic as the substance of chapters on dialectic and discourse in works of Islamic scholars, emphasizing that it is a tool not an independent discipline. [Note: Al-Ghazali consistently treats logic as a tool; later Ash'ari theologians adopted this view.]
المحك (al-miḥakk): The title of this book, meaning 'touchstone', symbolizing a criterion to test truth from falsehood. [Note: Al-Ghazali uses this term metaphorically; it is not a standard logical term.]

The Linguistic Root and Metaphor of al-Mihakk
Author analyzes the linguistic root and metaphor of the book's title.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace the etymology and metaphorical extension of a key term in Islamic logic from its root meaning to its technical usage.

Core Idea
The book's title is a metaphor: as a touchstone tests metals, logic tests truth.

Al-Ghazali begins his logical work by reflecting on its title. He unpacks the Arabic root ḥ-k-k, which means two things rubbing together. From this physical action, he derives the word 'miḥakk' – a tool for distinguishing pure gold from base metal. By naming his book 'al-Mihakk', he signals that logic serves as a tool to rub thoughts together and discern truth from falsehood. This lesson will guide you through his linguistic analysis and its deeper implication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the triliteral root
Locate the root letters (ḥ-k-k) in the passage. Al-Ghazali quotes Ibn Faris to establish the core meaning: two things rubbing against each other.
Root analysis is a standard method in Arabic lexicography.
2
Understand the noun of instrument pattern
The word 'miḥakk' follows the pattern mifʿal, which in Arabic is used for instruments. Al-Ghazali explains that this is a productive pattern for tools.
This morphological pattern is called ism āla.
3
Trace the real-world analogy
The author mentions goldsmiths using a stone (touchstone) to test metals. This concrete example is the source domain for the metaphor.
The touchstone reveals quality by rubbing the metal against it.
4
Apply the metaphor to logic
Al-Ghazali extends the touchstone metaphor to the book: 'your sight and thought need a touchstone by which they rub until correct is known from error.' Logic is the tool that tests reasoning.
The book itself serves as that touchstone for the reader.
5
Confirm the book's purpose
The name is not arbitrary; it encapsulates the book's function as a criterion (miḥakk) for distinguishing truth from falsehood in arguments.
This mirrors the goldsmith's use of the stone to distinguish pure gold from base.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تأمل في اسم الكتاب
يقول العلامة ابن فارس في مقاييس اللغة ( حك ) : ( الحاء والكاف أصل واحد ؛ وهو أن يلتقي شيئان يتمرّس كل واحد منهما بصاحبه ) فنظرك وفكرك كأنهما بحاجة إلى مِحَكٍّ يتمرَّسان به حتى يُعرف الصواب من الخطأ ، فكلمة ( مِحَك ) إنما هي اسم آلة على وزن ( مِفْعَل ) دالة على هذا المعنى ، وهو وزن قياسي لكل ما لم يرد فيه اسم آلة جامد ، وقد كان الصاغة يتخذون حجراً وينعتونه المِحَكَّ ، يعرفون به الإبريز من الخسيس ، وفي المثل : بحجر المِحَكِّ . وقال ابن الأثير في المثل السائر في صفة هذا الحجر : ( ومُدَّرِعٍ مِنْ صنعةِ الليل بُرده يُفَوَّقُ طوراً بالنضار ويطلس إذا سألوه عن عويصين أشكلا أجاب بما أعيا الورى وهو أخرس )
Reflection on the name of the book. Ibn Faris says in Maqāyīs al-Lugha (entry: ḥ-k): 'The ḥā' and kāf are a single root, which is that two things meet, each rubbing against the other.' So your sight and your thought are, as it were, in need of a touchstone by which they rub until correct is known from error. The word 'miḥakk' is a noun of instrument on the pattern 'mifʿal', indicating this meaning, and it is a qiyāsī pattern for everything for which no fixed noun of instrument has been reported. The goldsmiths used to take a stone and call it al-miḥakk, by which they distinguish pure gold from base. And in the proverb: 'By the touchstone'. And Ibn al-Athīr said in al-Mathal al-Sāʾir in describing this stone: 'And one clad in the craft of the night, his garment sometimes gilded and sometimes erased; when asked about two difficult matters that confused, he answered what baffled all, while he is mute.'
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a reflection on the title of the book, al-Mihakk. Al-Ghazali begins by citing Ibn Faris's lexicographical analysis of the root ḥ-k-k, which denotes two things rubbing together. He then applies this to the book's purpose: one's sight and thought need a touchstone to rub against in order to discern truth from error. He explains that 'miḥakk' is a noun of instrument on the pattern mifʿal, which is productive in Arabic. He gives a real-world example: goldsmiths use a touchstone to distinguish pure gold from base metal. Finally, he quotes a poem describing the touchstone as a mute stone that reveals the quality of gold and answers difficult questions. This reinforces the idea that the book serves as a criterion for sound thought.

Etymology and Purpose of 'al-Mihakk'
Author explains the root of 'mihakk' and uses a poetic metaphor to illustrate testing truth from falsehood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the literal and metaphorical meaning of 'mihakk' and its role as a touchstone for truth in Islamic logic.

Core Idea
The mihakk is a touchstone for gold and a metaphor for the mind's tool to distinguish truth from falsehood.

This lesson introduces the title of the book, 'al-Mihakk', exploring its linguistic roots and the powerful metaphor it embodies. Understanding this term sets the stage for the entire science of logic as a tool for testing arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the root meaning
The author explains that the root kaf implies two things meeting and rubbing against each other. Recognize how this physical action relates to testing and discernment.
2
Analyze the grammatical pattern
'mihakk' is on the pattern mif'al, the standard Arabic pattern for nouns of instrument. Understand how this pattern indicates a tool designed for a specific function.
3
Connect to goldsmiths' practice
Historically, goldsmiths used a touchstone called al-mihakk to test gold and distinguish pure from impure. Grasp the analogy: just as the stone reveals pure gold, logic reveals sound reasoning.
4
Explore the poetic metaphor by Ibn al-Athir
The stone is described as silent yet capable of answering difficult questions. Reflect on how the 'Mihakk' book serves as an authoritative arbiter in debates, revealing truth when consulted.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والكاف أصل واحد؛ وهو أن يلتقي شيئان يتمرس كل واحد منهما بصاحبه. فنظرك وفكرك كأنهما بحاجة إلى محل يتمرسان به حتى يعرف الصواب من الخطأ. فكلمة (محك) إنما هي اسم آلة على وزن (مفعل) دالة على هذا المعنى، وهو وزن قياسي لكل ما لم يرد فيه اسم آلة جامد. وقد كان الصاغة يتخذون حجرا وينعتونه المحك، يعرفون به الإبريز من الخسيس. وفي المثل بحجر المحك. لابن الأثير في صفة هذا الحجر: ومدرع من صنعة الليل برده يفوق طورا بالنضار ويطلس إذا سألوه عن عويصين أشكلا أجاب بما أعيا الورى وهو أخرس.
The kaf is one root; it is that two things meet, each rubbing against the other. Your sight and thought are as if they need a place to rub against until correct is distinguished from error. So the word (mihakk) is indeed a noun of instrument on the pattern (mif'al) indicating this meaning, and it is a standard pattern for every solid noun of instrument not otherwise prescribed. The goldsmiths used to take a stone and call it al-mihakk, by which they recognized pure gold from base. And in the proverb about the stone al-mihakk. Ibn al-Athir described this stone: 'And a wearer of a garment made from the work of night, his cloak, he gilds at times with gold and silvers, when asked about two perplexities that are ambiguous, he answers with what confounds people while he is mute.'
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage explains the etymology and metaphorical meaning of the term 'al-Mihakk' as the title of this book. The author begins by noting that the root kaf has a basic meaning of two things meeting and rubbing against each other. He then analogizes this to the function of the intellect (nazar and fikr) which needs a medium to test and thereby distinguish truth from falsehood. The word 'mihakk' follows the pattern mif‘al, which is the standard Arabic pattern for nouns of instrument. Historically, goldsmiths used a specific stone called al-mihakk to test gold and distinguish pure from impure. Finally, the author cites a poetic description by Ibn al-Athir that likens the touchstone to a silent object that, when asked about difficult problems, gives answers that confound people—implying that this book serves a similar role in testing arguments and revealing the truth.

Four Differences between al-Mi'yar and al-Mihakk
Author enumerates four key differences between al-Ghazali's two logical works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate al-Ghazali's two logical works (al-Mi'yar and al-Mihakk) based on their approach to terminology, length, examples, and unique content.

Core Idea
Al-Mi'yar and al-Mihakk serve different pedagogical functions despite both being works of logic.

In this lesson, we explore the four key differences that al-Ghazali himself highlights between his two major logical works. Understanding these differences helps you choose the right text for your level and goal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first difference
Scan the text for the first difference: al-Mihakk avoids philosophical terminology while al-Mi'yar embraces it.
Consider why al-Ghazali would make this choice.
2
Identify the second difference
Find the second difference: conciseness versus expansiveness.
What does this tell you about the intended audience?
3
Identify the third difference
Find the third difference: abundance of examples vs. necessary examples only.
How does this affect learning?
4
Identify the fourth difference
Find the fourth difference: each book contains unique issues not in the other.
What does this imply about the comprehensive nature of each work?
5
Apply to your own study
Based on these differences, decide which work you would consult first as a beginner.
Justify your choice using the differences.
